</tr>
</table>
<p>Late on July 15, the NHC highlighted a low-pressure trough over the central Atlantic as having the potential to develop into a tropical cyclone in the coming days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> The disturbance began to show signs of organization early on July 17,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> and data from a reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system confirmed the development of Tropical Storm Don around 21:00 UTC that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> The storm's overall appearance improved over subsequent hours up until around 09:00 UTC, as a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a>, accompanied by significant clusters of lightning, became pronounced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-59">[57]</a></sup> Don attained its peak intensity at this time, characterised by winds of approximately 50 mph (85 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-59">[57]</a></sup> The next plane to investigate the cyclone a few hours later, however, found that the system's center had become less defined, and that sustained wind speeds had decreased to about 40 mph (65 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> A combination of reconnaissance data and surface observations from the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> indicated that Don opened up into a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> around 03:00 UTC on July 19, as it entered the eastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Emily">Tropical Storm Emily</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Emily">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg"><img alt="Emily 2017-07-31 1555Z.jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="3000" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/150px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/225px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/300px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emily_2017_track.png"><img alt="Emily 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/150px-Emily_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/225px-Emily_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/300px-Emily_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 31 – August 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1005 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In late July, a dissipating <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">cold front</a> extended into the northeastern Gulf of Mexico, where the NHC began forecasting the development of an area of low pressure over the next day on July 30. Any development was expected to be slow due to land proximity and marginal upper-level winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> Contrary to predictions, a rapid period of organization occurred over the next 24 hours and the system was deemed as Tropical Depression Six at 09:00 UTC on July 31,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> strengthening into Tropical Storm Emily just two hours later. After attaining its peak intensity with winds of 45 mph (75 km/h) and a minimum pressure of 1,005 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millibar" title="Millibar">mbar</a> (29.7 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inches_of_mercury" title="Inches of mercury">inHg</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> Emily made landfall on <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Island" title="Anna Maria Island">Anna Maria Island</a> around 14:45 UTC. Weakening quickly ensued, and later that day the circulation of Emily became elongated as it was downgraded to a tropical depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> The increasingly disrupted system later moved off the <a href="/wiki/First_Coast" title="First Coast">First Coast</a> of Florida into the western Atlantic early the next day, accelerating northeastwards before becoming embedded within a frontal zone early on August 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the classification of Tropical Storm Emily, Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> for 31 counties to ensure residents were provided with the necessary resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> The storm spawned an EF0 tornado near Bradenton. The tornado was on the ground for about 1.3 mi (2.1 km) and destroyed two barns and a few greenhouses, while an engineered wall collapsed, leaving about $96,000 in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> On August 1, torrential rains related to Emily impacted parts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami_Beach" title="Miami Beach">Miami Beach</a>, with accumulations reaching 6.97 in (177 mm) in 3.5 hours, of which 2.17 in (55 mm) fell in just 30 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Coinciding with high tide the deluge overwhelmed flood pumps, with three of them shutting down due to lightning-induced power outages, and resulted in significant flash floods. Multiple buildings suffered water damage, with some having 2.5 ft (0.76 m) of standing water. One person was hospitalized after becoming stuck in flood waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> Portions of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Downtown_Miami" title="Greater Downtown Miami">Downtown Miami</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Brickell" title="Brickell">Brickell</a>, were also heavily affected; numerous vehicles became stranded in flooded roadways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Franklin">Hurricane Franklin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Franklin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg"><img alt="Franklin 2017-08-09 1854Z.jpg" data-file-height="3480" data-file-width="2501" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/150px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/225px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/300px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franklin_2017_track.png"><img alt="Franklin 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Franklin_2017_track.png/150px-Franklin_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Franklin_2017_track.png/225px-Franklin_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Franklin_2017_track.png/300px-Franklin_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 7 – August 10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>85 mph (140 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  981 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin" title="Hurricane Franklin">Hurricane Franklin</a></div>
<p>The NHC began tracking a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> in the southeastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> for possible <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">development</a> on August 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> After organizing for a few days, advisories were initiated on Potential Tropical Cyclone Seven at 21:00 UTC on August 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d1_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-d1-74">[72]</a></sup> The disturbance became Tropical Storm Franklin at 03:00 UTC on August 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d2_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-d2-75">[73]</a></sup> After strengthening into a moderate tropical storm, Franklin made its first landfall near Pulticub, Mexico at 03:00 UTC on August 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1stlandfallfranklin_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-1stlandfallfranklin-76">[74]</a></sup> The cyclone weakened considerably while over the peninsula, however its satellite presentation remained well-defined, with the inner core tightening up considerably.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d7_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-d7-77">[75]</a></sup> Later that day, Franklin emerged into the Bay of Campeche, and immediately began strengthening again, becoming a hurricane late on August 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Five hours after peaking in intensity with winds of 85 mph (140 km/h) and a pressure of 981 mbar (28.97 inHg),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> Franklin made landfall in <a href="/wiki/Vega_de_Alatorre" title="Vega de Alatorre">Lechuguillas, Mexico</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> and thereafter began to rapidly weaken. By 15:00 UTC on August 10, Franklin had dissipated as a tropical cyclone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> However, its mid-level circulation remained intact and later contributed to the formation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Jova_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Jova (2017)">Tropical Storm Jova</a> in the Eastern Pacific early on August 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jova_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jova-82">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Immediately upon classification of Franklin as a potential tropical cyclone, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm_warning" title="Tropical storm warning">tropical storm warnings</a> were issued for much of the eastern side of the Yucatán Peninsula on August 6;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-d1_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-d1-74">[72]</a></sup> a small portion of the coastline was upgraded to a hurricane watch with the possibility of Franklin nearing hurricane intensity as it approached the coastline the next night. Approximately 330 people were reported as going into storm shelters, and around 2,200 relocated from the islands near the coastline to farther inland in advance of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-impacts1_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-impacts1-83">[81]</a></sup> In the Mexican part of the peninsula, damage was reported as having being minimal, mainly in Belize as the storm tracked slightly more northwards then expected, lessening impacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-impacts1_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-impacts1-83">[81]</a></sup> Nonetheless, some areas received up to a foot of rain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Gert">Hurricane Gert</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Gert">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg"><img alt="Gert 2017-08-16 Suomi NPP.jpg" data-file-height="3300" data-file-width="2270" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Gert_2017-08-16_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gert_2017_track.png"><img alt="Gert 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gert_2017_track.png/150px-Gert_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gert_2017_track.png/225px-Gert_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Gert_2017_track.png/300px-Gert_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 13 – August 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>105 mph (165 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  967 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 2, the NHC began monitoring a tropical wave and its associated convection over the western coast of Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> As the disturbance tracked west-northwest, its structure changed little in organization, but environmental conditions were expected to support the formation of a tropical cyclone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Instead, the system remained poorly defined and entered a less conducive environment east of the Leeward Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> After progressing into the southwestern Atlantic several days later, the wave encountered more favorable upper-level winds and began to show signs of organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> Following the formation of a well-defined circulation, the disturbance was upgraded to a tropical depression at 03:00 UTC on August 13;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> by 21:00 UTC that afternoon, it intensified into Tropical Storm Gert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> At 03:00 UTC on August 15, Gert intensified to a Category 1 hurricane with maximum sustained winds of 75 mph (120 km/h), making it the second hurricane of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> Accelerating east-northeastwards, Gert peaked as a Category 2 system early on August 17 at an unusually high latitude of 40°N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> Thereafter, Gert began to rapidly weaken as it exited the warm waters of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> Just 12 hours after achieving peak intensity, Gert weakened below hurricane status and transitioned to an extratropical cyclone well east of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two people drowned due to strong rip currents produced by the hurricane: one in the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Banks" title="Outer Banks">Outer Banks</a> of North Carolina, and the other in <a href="/wiki/Nantucket,_Massachusetts" title="Nantucket, Massachusetts">Nantucket, Massachusetts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hurricane Harvey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png"><img alt="Harvey 2017-08-25 2231Z.png" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="1800" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png/150px-Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png/225px-Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png/300px-Harvey_2017-08-25_2231Z.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harvey_2017_track.png"><img alt="Harvey 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Harvey_2017_track.png/150px-Harvey_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Harvey_2017_track.png/225px-Harvey_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Harvey_2017_track.png/300px-Harvey_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 17 – September 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 mph (215 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  938 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">Hurricane Harvey</a></div>
<p>The NHC began monitoring an area of low pressure southwest of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> on August 13, which was expected to merge with a tropical wave that just emerged off the coast of Africa, within a few days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> Instead the two systems remained separate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> with the first low pressure area coalescing into a potential tropical cyclone by 15:00 UTC on August 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> A reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system was able to locate a well-defined circulation, and the disturbance was upgraded to Tropical Storm Harvey accordingly six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> On a westward course into the Caribbean Sea, the storm was plagued by relentless wind shear, and it degenerated to an open tropical wave south of Hispaniola, by 03:00 UTC on August 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> Harvey's remnants continued into the Bay of Campeche, where more conducive environmental conditions led to the re-designation of a tropical depression, around 15:00 UTC on August 23, and subsequent intensification into a tropical storm by 04:00 UTC on the next morning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> The cyclone began a period of rapid intensification shortly thereafter, attaining hurricane intensity by 17:00 UTC on August 24,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-104">[102]</a></sup> Category 3 strength around 19:00 UTC on August 25,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> and Category 4 intensity by 23:00 UTC on that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-104">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harvey crossed the shore between <a href="/wiki/Port_Aransas,_Texas" title="Port Aransas, Texas">Port Aransas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Port_O%27Connor,_Texas" title="Port O'Connor, Texas">Port O'Connor, Texas</a> around 03:00 UTC on August 26, possessing maximum winds of 130 mph (215 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> The storm gradually spun down, becoming a tropical storm around 18:00 UTC on August 26, as it meandered across southeastern Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> A light steering pattern caused the storm to emerge into the Gulf of Mexico on August 28,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> but a turn toward the north-northeast brought it ashore west of <a href="/wiki/Cameron,_Louisiana" title="Cameron, Louisiana">Cameron, Louisiana</a>, as a weak tropical storm around 09:00 UTC on August 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> The system weakened to a tropical depression over central Louisiana late that day before losing tropical characteristics over central Tennessee early on September 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rockport,_Texas" title="Rockport, Texas">Rockport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulton,_Texas" title="Fulton, Texas">Fulton</a>, and the surrounding cities bore the brunt of Harvey's eyewall as it moved ashore in Texas. Numerous structures were heavily damaged or destroyed, boats were tossed or capsized, power poles were leant or snapped, and trees were downed. As debris covered roadways and cellphone service was compromised, communication to the hardest-hit locales was severed. One person was killed in Rockport after a fire began in his home, and approximately a dozen people were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twc_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-twc-112">[110]</a></sup> Farther northeast, dire predictions of potentially catastrophic flooding came to fruition in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">Houston</a> and nearby locales, where floodwaters submerged interstates, forced residents to their attics and roofs, and overwhelmed emergency lines. The National Weather Service <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweeted</a>, "This event is unprecedented &amp; all impacts are unknown &amp; beyond anything experienced..." At least 30 people were killed in the Houston area due to flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TNYT_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-TNYT-113">[111]</a></sup> In addition to the flooding, Harvey spawned several tornadoes around Houston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> Preliminary estimates place the damage caused by Harvey between $65<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIR_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-AIR-115">[113]</a></sup> and $200 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200billion_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-200billion-116">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quealy_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quealy-117">[115]</a></sup> Harvey killed 84 people, including 1 in <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdema_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-cdema-118">[116]</a></sup> and 83 in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashPost_death_toll_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-WashPost_death_toll-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> The storm produced 64.58 in (1,640 mm) of rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, the highest-ever rainfall total for any tropical cyclone in the United States and the third-highest rainfall total for a tropical cyclone in the Atlantic basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[nb 3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Harvey was the first major hurricane to strike the United States since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, ending the record-long drought that lasted 4,323 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup> It is the most intense tropical cyclone to move ashore the mainland since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">Hurricane Charley</a> in <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004</a>, the first Category 4 hurricane to make landfall in Texas since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carla" title="Hurricane Carla">Hurricane Carla</a> in <a href="/wiki/1961_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1961 Atlantic hurricane season">1961</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[122]</a></sup> Harvey is the first hurricane to affect the Mainland or Territorial U.S this season, and is overall the costliest one as well, despite the fact that it's weaker than the other ones.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Irma">Hurricane Irma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hurricane Irma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg"><img alt="Irma 2017-09-06 1745Z.jpg" data-file-height="9600" data-file-width="7200" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg/150px-Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg/225px-Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg/300px-Irma_2017-09-06_1745Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irma_2017_track.png"><img alt="Irma 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/150px-Irma_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/225px-Irma_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irma_2017_track.png/300px-Irma_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 30 – September 12</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>185 mph (295 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  914 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a></div>
<p>A westward-moving tropical wave, first monitored over western Africa on August 26,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup> organized into Tropical Storm Irma around 15:00 UTC on August 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[124]</a></sup> Amid an environment of low wind shear and warm ocean temperatures, the newly formed cyclone moved generally westward while intensifying. A reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system east of the Caribbean on September 5 found the cyclone at Category 5 intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup> With a clear eye surrounded by a ring of extremely deep convection, Irma attained its peak intensity with winds of 185 mph (295 km/h) later that day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[126]</a></sup> and maintained this intensity as it moved through the northern Leeward Islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[127]</a></sup> Some weakening occurred south of the Bahamas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[128]</a></sup> but the cyclone regained Category 5 intensity before making landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Sabana-Camag%C3%BCey_Archipelago" title="Sabana-Camagüey Archipelago">Sabana-Camagüey Archipelago</a> of Cuba around 03:00 UTC on September 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup> Land interaction disrupted the storm temporarily,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup> but once again it strengthened to acquire winds of 130 mph (215 km/h), before making landfall in <a href="/wiki/Cudjoe_Key,_Florida" title="Cudjoe Key, Florida">Cudjoe Key</a> of the Florida Keys early on September 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[131]</a></sup> A few hours later, it struck <a href="/wiki/Marco_Island,_Florida" title="Marco Island, Florida">Marco Island, Florida</a>, with winds of 115 mph (185 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[132]</a></sup> Irma continued north and west, steadily weakening over the Southeastern United States before losing tropical characteristics in Georgia, early on September 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>With peak winds of 185 mph (295 km/h), Irma is the strongest Atlantic storm outside of the Gulf of Mexico or Caribbean Sea on record, and is the 11th most intense hurricane on record in the Atlantic basin. Maintaining peak intensity for 37 consecutive hours, Irma is the only tropical cyclone on record worldwide to have had winds that intense for so long. As the storm moved through the northern Leeward Islands, it became the only Category 5 to make a direct impact there; its landfall intensity ties it with the 1935 Labor Day hurricane as the strongest landfalling cyclone on record in the Atlantic. Two Category 4 hurricanes, Harvey and Irma, struck the United States in the span of two weeks; this marks the first time the country has suffered two landfalls of such intensity during the same hurricane season, in recorded history. Lastly, Irma accrued the third-highest Accumulated Cyclone Energy index on record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the aftermath of Irma, development on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> was described as being "95% destroyed" by respective political leaders, with 1,400 people feared homeless in Barbuda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[135]</a></sup> So far, Irma has resulted in at least 124 deaths, including 44 across the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, and 80 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_death_toll_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters_death_toll-139">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuclear_landscape_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-nuclear_landscape-140">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_AFP_death_toll_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_AFP_death_toll-141">[138]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Jose">Hurricane Jose</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hurricane Jose">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Jose 2017-09-08 1425Z (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="319" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Jose_2017-09-08_1425Z_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jose_2017_track.png"><img alt="Jose 2017 track.png" data-file-height="2513" data-file-width="3000" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jose_2017_track.png/150px-Jose_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jose_2017_track.png/225px-Jose_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jose_2017_track.png/300px-Jose_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 5 – September 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>155 mph (250 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  938 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose (2017)</a></div>
<p>A westward-moving tropical wave exited the west coast of Africa on August 31,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[139]</a></sup> organizing into Tropical Storm Jose over the open eastern Atlantic by 15:00 UTC on September 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[140]</a></sup> The quickly-strengthening cyclone attained hurricane intensity late on September 6,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[141]</a></sup> reached major hurricane strength late on September 7,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[142]</a></sup> and ultimately peaked as a Category 4 with winds of 155 mph (250 km/h) early on September 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[143]</a></sup> Moderate wind shear weakened the cyclone as it conducted a slow clockwise loop between Bermuda and the Caribbean Sea and eventually moved north ahead of an approaching trough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[144]</a></sup> Steering currents collapsed by early on September 21, causing the system to stall offshore the Northeastern United States as a weakening tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[145]</a></sup> With a rain shield in the northern and northwestern semicircles accompanied by a lack of deep convection over the center, the NHC declared Jose a post-tropical cyclone around 03:00 UTC on September 22, ending advisories once the storm's tropical storm-force winds moved off the New England coast at 21:00 UTC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government of <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a> began efforts on September 8 to evacuate the entire island prior to Jose's anticipated arrival, as most structures on the island had been heavily damaged or destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[148]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Katia">Hurricane Katia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hurricane Katia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg"><img alt="Katia 2017-09-08 1930Z.jpg" data-file-height="5872" data-file-width="4536" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg/150px-Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg/225px-Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg/300px-Katia_2017-09-08_1930Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katia_2017_track.png"><img alt="Katia 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Katia_2017_track.png/150px-Katia_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Katia_2017_track.png/225px-Katia_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Katia_2017_track.png/300px-Katia_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 5 – September 9</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>105 mph (165 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  972 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A trough was present over the southwestern Gulf of Mexico on September 3, producing a widespread area of thunderstorms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[149]</a></sup> Two days later, a distinct low pressure area formed about 50 mi (80 km) east of <a href="/wiki/Tampico" title="Tampico">Tampico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[150]</a></sup> At 21:00 UTC that day, the NHC designated the system as Tropical Depression Thirteen after an organized area of convection formed over the center. Located in an area of weak steering currents, the depression drifted slowly eastward. With gradually decreasing wind shear and warm water temperatures, the system intensified into Tropical Storm Katia on September 6, as the convection became better organized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[152]</a></sup> Later that day, an aircraft reconnaissance flight into the storm found a partial <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye wall</a> and surface winds of 76 mph (122 km/h); on that basis, the NHC upgraded Katia to hurricane status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[153]</a></sup> The convection organized into a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> as the system stalled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[154]</a></sup> Late in the evening of September 8, Katia made landfall north of <a href="/wiki/Tecolutla" title="Tecolutla">Tecolutla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> as a weak Category 1 storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup> The system rapidly dissipated over land on September 9. Katia's remnants traveled across Central America and later emerged over the Pacific Ocean, where redevelopment ensued. Tropical Depression Fifteen-E formed, which later strengthened into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Otis_(2017)" title="Hurricane Otis (2017)">Hurricane Otis</a> about a week later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>In preparation for Katia, over 4,000 residents were evacuated from the states of <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[157]</a></sup> Tourists left coastal towns, emergency shelters were opened, and storm drains were cleared before the onset of heavy rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[158]</a></sup> Two fatalities were reported in <a href="/wiki/Xalapa" title="Xalapa">Xalapa</a> from mudslides, while a third man was swept away by floodwaters in <a href="/wiki/Jalcomulco" title="Jalcomulco">Jalcomulco</a>. States of emergency were declared for 40 out of a total 53 municipalities that reported minor damage from mudslides and flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[159]</a></sup> About 77,000 residents were left without power at the height of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[160]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Lee">Hurricane Lee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hurricane Lee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg"><img alt="Lee 2017-09-27 1450Z.jpg" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="4500" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg/150px-Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg/225px-Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg/300px-Lee_2017-09-27_1450Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lee_2017_track.png"><img alt="Lee 2017 track.png" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lee_2017_track.png/150px-Lee_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lee_2017_track.png/225px-Lee_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Lee_2017_track.png/300px-Lee_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 15 – September 30</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>115 mph (185 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  962 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave moved off the coast of Africa on September 13. Contrary to predictions of only gradual organization over the following days,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[161]</a></sup> the system rapidly organized, becoming Tropical Depression Fourteen at 03:00 UTC on September 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[162]</a></sup> The NHC upgraded the system to Tropical Storm Lee at 15:00 UTC on the next day, based on an increase in deep convection and an <a href="/wiki/Scatterometer" title="Scatterometer">advanced scatterometer</a> (ASCAT) pass which indicated that it was producing minimal tropical-storm-force winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[163]</a></sup> After encountering wind shear, Lee gradually weakened into a tropical depression early on September 17 before degenerating into a remnant low two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[165]</a></sup> The NHC monitored the remnants of Lee intermittently for several days, but regeneration was not considered likely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[167]</a></sup> However, the mid-level remnants of the cyclone became intertwined with an upper-level trough; a deep burst of convection led to a new surface circulation, and by 21:00 UTC on September 22, the system reorganized into Tropical Depression Lee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[168]</a></sup> It intensified into a tropical storm six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>A compact cyclone, Lee organized as small curved bands wrapped into a small cluster of central convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[170]</a></sup> A microwave pass around 21:00 UTC on September 23 indicated the formation of a ring of shallow to moderate convection around the center, often a harbinger of rapid intensification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[171]</a></sup> Indeed, by 06:30 UTC the next morning, the presence of an eye on satellite imagery prompted the NHC to abruptly upgrade Lee to a hurricane as it moved erratically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[172]</a></sup> After attaining winds of 90 mph (150 km/h), the storm weakened slightly due to moderate southeasterly wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[173]</a></sup> By 09:00 UTC on September 26, however, the storm attained Category 2 strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[174]</a></sup> An eyewall replacement cycle that night led to the emergence of a larger eye surrounded by cold cloud tops, and by 15:00 UTC on September 27, Lee attained its peak as a Category 3 hurricane with winds of 115 mph (185 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[175]</a></sup> The system recurved northeast after peak intensity and quickly succumbed to strong northerly wind shear and progressively cooler ocean waters;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[176]</a></sup> it weakened below major hurricane strength by 03:00 UTC on September 28,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[177]</a></sup> fell below hurricane strength by 15:00 UTC on September 29,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[178]</a></sup> and degenerated to a post-tropical cyclone by 09:00 UTC on September 30, after lacking deep convection for over 12 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[179]</a></sup> On October 1, Lee's remnant was absorbed by another extratropical cyclone to the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-October_1_weather_map_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-October_1_weather_map-183">[180]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Maria">Hurricane Maria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hurricane Maria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_(gallery).jpg"><img alt="Maria 2017-09-19 1742Z (gallery).jpg" data-file-height="6272" data-file-width="4808" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_%28gallery%29.jpg/150px-Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_%28gallery%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_%28gallery%29.jpg/225px-Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_%28gallery%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_%28gallery%29.jpg/300px-Maria_2017-09-19_1742Z_%28gallery%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017_track.png"><img alt="Maria 2017 track.png" data-file-height="2290" data-file-width="3000" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/150px-Maria_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/225px-Maria_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/300px-Maria_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 16 – September 30</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>175 mph (280 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  908 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a></div>
<p>On September 13, the NHC began monitoring a tropical wave southwest of Cabo Verde.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[181]</a></sup> The disturbance moved west, organizing into a potential tropical cyclone at 15:00 UTC on September 16 and Tropical Storm Maria six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[183]</a></sup> On a west-northwest course, Maria intensified at an exceptional rate and attained Category 5 strength around 23:45 UTC on September 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[184]</a></sup> After striking Dominica at that intensity a little over an hour later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[185]</a></sup> the storm weakened slightly as it entered the eastern Caribbean Sea; amid favorable conditions, however, Maria regained Category 5 intensity and eventually reached peak winds of 175 mph (280 km/h) late on September 19.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[186]</a></sup> Around 08:00 UTC on September 20, the eyewall of Maria struck Vieques,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[187]</a></sup> and a little over two hours later, the core of the storm made landfall near Yabucoa, Puerto Rico, with winds of 155 mph (250 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[188]</a></sup> Land interaction caused a significant degration in Maria's structure, and it weakened to a Category 2 hurricane while moving offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[189]</a></sup> Growing in size and curving north, Maria regained Category 3 strength and maintained this intensity for several days before entering a less conducive environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[190]</a></sup> After fluctuating between tropical storm and minimal hurricane strength off the coastline of North Carolina,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[191]</a></sup> the system turned sharply east away from the United States and ultimately transitioned into an extratropical cyclone over the far northern Atlantic on September 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dominica sustained catastrophic damage from Maria, with nearly every structure on the island damaged or destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[194]</a></sup> Surrounding islands were also dealt a devastating blow, with reports of flooding, downed trees, and damaged buildings. Puerto Rico also suffered catastrophic damage. The island's electric grid was devastated, leaving all 3.4 million residents without power. Many structures were leveled, while floodwaters trapped thousands of citizens. The United States National Guard, Coast Guard, Army Corps of Engineers, and other like units worked to administer aid and assist in search and rescue operations. However, the U.S. federal government response was criticized for its delay in waiving the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Marine_Act_of_1920" title="Merchant Marine Act of 1920">Jones Act</a>, a statute which prevented Puerto Rico from receiving aid on ships from non-U.S. flagged vessels. Along the coastline of the United States, tropical storm-force gusts cut power to hundreds of citizens; rip currents offshore led to three deaths and numerous water rescues. Estimates of damage from Maria range from $40 billion to $95 billion, mainly in Puerto Rico, and the governor of the territory believes the storm did $90 billion in damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90_billion_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-90_billion-198">[195]</a></sup> The death toll as currently reported stands at 78, with 30 killed in Dominica, 5 in the Dominican Republic, 2 in Guadeloupe, 3 in Haiti, 34 in Puerto Rico, 1 in the United States Virgin Islands, and 3 in the Contiguous United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34_in_Puerto_Rico_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-34_in_Puerto_Rico-199">[196]</a></sup></p>

<p>On October 3, 2017, a broad area of low pressure formed in the southwestern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup> The disturbance quickly organized, and on October 4, the NHC announced that the disturbance had strengthened into Tropical Depression Sixteen, and began issuing advisories on the storm.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_storm_information">Current storm information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Current storm information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of 5:00 p.m. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EDT</a> (21:00 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>) October 4, Tropical Depression Sixteen is located within 20 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> of <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;params=12.5_N_-82.5_E_dim:130km&amp;title=Sixteen"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">12°30′N</span> <span class="longitude">82°30′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">12.5°N 82.5°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">12.5; -82.5</span></span><span style="display:none">﻿ (<span class="fn org">Sixteen</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>, about 55 miles (85 km) <a href="/wiki/Points_of_the_compass" title="Points of the compass">W</a> of <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_(island)" title="San Andrés (island)">San Andrés Island</a>, and about 180 miles (290 km) <a href="/wiki/Points_of_the_compass" title="Points of the compass">south-southeast</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_Gracias_a_Dios" title="Cabo Gracias a Dios">Cabo Gracias a Dios</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>/<a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> border. Maximum sustained winds are 30 knots (35 mph; 55 km/h), with gusts up to 40 knots (45 mph; 65 km/h). The minimum barometric pressure is 1005 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>; 29.68 <a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">inHg</a>), and the system is moving northwest at 6 knots (7 mph; 11 km/h).</p>
<p><br/>
For latest official information, see:</p>
<ul>
<li>The NHC's <a class="external text" href="http://www.nhc.noaa.gov/text/refresh/MIATCPAT1+shtml/" rel="nofollow">latest public advisory on Tropical Depression Sixteen</a></li>
<li>The NHC's <a class="external text" href="http://www.nhc.noaa.gov/text/refresh/MIATCMAT1+shtml/" rel="nofollow">latest forecast advisory on Tropical Depression Sixteen</a></li>
<li>The NHC's <a class="external text" href="http://www.nhc.noaa.gov/text/refresh/MIATCDAT1+shtml/" rel="nofollow">latest forecast discussion on Tropical Depression Sixteen</a></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_systems">Other systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Other systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7057" data-file-width="5025" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg/170px-10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg/255px-10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg/340px-10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:10L_2017-08-28_1750Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Potential Tropical Cyclone Ten near the Carolinas on August 28</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A long-tracked tropical wave was designated as Potential Tropical Cyclone Ten, while it was located northeast of Florida on August 27. The NHC gave this disturbance a 90% chance of becoming a tropical cyclone within the next 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[198]</a></sup> However, the system did not attain any more tropical characteristics, and it began to undergo an extratropical transition. Consequently, the NHC issued its last advisory on the system at 21:00 UTC on August 29, declaring the system to be an extratropical low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[199]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>
<p>The following list of names will be used for named storms that form in the North Atlantic in 2017. Any retired names will be announced by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO) in the spring of 2018. The names not retired from this list will not be used again until the 2023 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[200]</a></sup> This is the same list used in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2011 Atlantic hurricane season">2011 season</a>, with the exception of the name Irma, which replaced <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene" title="Hurricane Irene">Irene</a>; Irma was previously used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Irma_(1978)" title="Tropical Storm Irma (1978)">1978 season</a>.</p>

<li><span style="color:#666666">Vince <i>(unused)</i></span></li>
<li><span style="color:#666666">Whitney <i>(unused)</i></span></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>The usage of the name "Don" in July garnered some negative attention relating to <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>. <a href="/wiki/Max_Mayfield" title="Max Mayfield">Max Mayfield</a>, former director of the National Hurricane Center, clarified that the name had no relation to Trump and was chosen in 2006 as a replacement for <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dennis" title="Hurricane Dennis">Dennis</a>. Regardless, some outlets such as the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, "poked fun" at the name and Trump.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a table of all the storms that have formed in the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, affected areas, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2017 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">USD</a>.</p>

</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The totals represent the sum of the squares for every (sub)tropical storm's intensity of over 33 knots (38 mph, 61 km/h), divided by 10,000. Calculations are provided at <a href="/wiki/Talk:2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season/ACE_calcs" title="Talk:2017 Atlantic hurricane season/ACE calcs">Talk:2017 Atlantic hurricane season/ACE calcs</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It should be noted that Arlene would likely not have been detected without the help of satellites, and there may well have been other similar storms this early in the year in the pre-satellite era (1966 and before).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Higher rainfall totals occurred during the <a href="/wiki/1909_Greater_Antilles_hurricane" title="1909 Greater Antilles hurricane">Greater Antilles hurricane</a> of 1909; peaking at 135.00 in (3,429 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Flora" title="Hurricane Flora">Hurricane Flora</a> of 1963; peaking at 100.39 in (2,550 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. For more information, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country" title="List of wettest tropical cyclones by country">List of wettest tropical cyclones by country</a>.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>
